text:
Okay, I am absolutely addicted to this salad.  However, I have made some changes to it.  First, I prefer bow tie pasta.  I think it gives it a little more visual appeal.  I also dry the pasta on paper towels after I drain it.  This keeps the moisture level down and allows the dressing to coat the pasta better.  I use fat free Miracle Whip to keep the fat content down.  I use four eggs instead of three.  I find the sugar is an important ingredient however, I only use about 1/4 to 1/2 cup.  I also use apple cider vinegar.  I don't add the red pepper because my husband doesn't like them but they do give it a great color.  We all love celery so I add extra and I also chop the leaves from the celery stalks and add those.  I also like to add in a little garlic salt.  It always seems to  make a lot of dressing so I mix in just enough to coat the pasta and let it sit over night.  I cover and fridge the remaining dressing.  Then, if it looks a little dry in the morning, I add more of the dressing.  This keeps it from being too liquidy.  

I have also added in a can of well drained tuna which gives it a great flavor and makes it more of a meal.  

The dressing also works great as a base for potato salad.  

YUM!!!

text:
What a wonderful, delicious recipe! I reduced the sugar a bit but next time will add even less. I think 1/4 or 1/3 cup will suit my families tastes. I had a hard time putting this recipe together since I found myself out of some ingredients. I subbed one cup of Marzetti's slaw dressing and one cup of Mayo for the Miracle Whip. I also chopped one small dill pickle and added a little pickle juice for the relish. Didn't have celery seed so that was left out. With summer coming up I can see myself making this many times over! Thank you for the post. By the way, for the poster that mentioned the restaurant, Das Dutch Haus in Ohio: I used to live in Pittsburgh and a highlight for us moms was to drive over to shop and eat at Das Dutch Haus. Ah, the memories. I loved the food there! :-) *Update* Made this again and used the salad dressing. Used celery salt instead of salt and celery seed. This is just so yummy! Made again and sprinkled with paprika and black pepper. Outstanding! For those of you that think that this is a little soupy, place in the fridge overnight and the noodles soak up some of the liquid. It is perfect the day after preparing!

text:
This is the recipe I use every time I make mac salad! I use real mayonnaise, Miracle Whip doesn't exist in my kitchen. Green pepper instead of red, cut the sugar to 1/2 cup, and no pickle relish. I add an extra hard boiled egg, shredded cheese, and I season the dressing with extra salt, pepper, garlic powder and a couple drops of Louisianna hot sauce for flavor. I cut the mustard to 1 Tbsp. Other good additions are diced ham or bacon. Amish macaroni salad is supposed to be sweet.

text:
As per other reviewers' remarks I cut the amount of dressing.  But pasta absorbs all moisture very quickly, becoming dry. So, if not eating the salad right away, I suggest following the recipe as is (I agree with reducing sugar to 1/4 c.)- add enough dressing to salad to satisfy immediate eating requirements- keep the rest for later. You will need it.
Also, another reviewer suggested adding cubed cheese - I don't think cheese adds anything to this recipe it's quite simply excellent as is.
Edit: I have now made this recipe dozens of times.  Yesterday I bought mayonaise instead of Miracle Whip-type salad dressing - in my opinion using mayo requires more sugar - I used a half cup.  Other than that - I'm still making it as above and getting raves from my guests and family.

Perhaps I should preface my review by saying I hate macaroni salad....just not a big fan, can easily walk away and not eat it.  Yuck.  My dad requested mac salad for Father's Day and I searched for the "right" recipe and found this.  OMG.  I just ate a bowl and it's fantastic.  And the flavors haven't even had a chance to meld.  And I hate mac salad!  I did make some changes, here they are:  I doubled the recipe and used 4-5 C uncooked whole grain elbows.  I diced a md green pepper, a md red pepper, a sm-md red onion, 6 celery ribs, and 4 dill pickle spears (no dill relish, I realized).  I used 6 hard boiled eggs.  In the dressing, I used Kraft Light Mayo w/Olive Oil, yellow mustard, 2/3C sugar (and I would not use anymore, perhaps would use less, maybe down to 1/3C even next time) and I didn't measure the white vinegar, just added a couple of splashes.  I also added  a healthy amt of dill pickle juice (2 good "splashes" from the jar).  I added the following seasonings (I did not measure, I just sort of sprinkled across the top to cover, not coat, twice):  garlic salt (and did not use regular salt then), dill weed, and crushed red pepper (about 8 shakes).  I did not use celery seed simply because I hate celery (and I purposefully cut the celery large so I can pick it out :)).  I WILL be making this again.  Thanks for making me a mac salad eater (though, wait, I prob shouldn't be thanking you for adding yet another high calorie "like" to my list!)!

This really is a fantastic macaroni salad. I did use several suggestions made by other reviewers... I added an extra hard-boiled egg (4 total), I reduced the sugar to 1/2C.(will reduce to 1/4C. next time and see how we like it) and I added only 1/2 the dressing (used Miracle Whip)to begin with. After refrigerating the salad all day I took it out, gave it a good stir, and added about 1/4 of the remaining dressing. This was perfect and didn't make it too "soupy". I will make this salad often...thanks so much for the great recipe!

This is my recipe that I sent in and use when I make mac salad.  The only thing is someone changed the way to do the mac.  Don't boil it for 8-10 minutes.  Get water boiling, put in mac, bring back to a boil, stir, turn off heat.  Leave covered for 10 minutes then drain and make salad.  That is what the recipe calls to do.

My husband LOVES Amish Macaroni Salad which is typically very sweet and saturated with dressing.  I gave this a try and am so glad I did!  This most certainly is colorful and flavorful.  Like others, I cut back on the sugar (a little over 1/4 cup) which was a good idea.  I used a vidalia onion finely chopped and half light Miracle Whip and half Hellman's light mayo.  I also added an additional hard boiled egg.  This definitely needs to set overnight so the dressing can get soaked up a bit by the macaroni but otherwise excellent!

text:
I'm so happy I stumbled upon this recipe. It truly is a great macaroni salad. Most of the ingredients, by themselves, I don't care for, but mixed into this salad, the flavors are so complimentary.  Per other reviews, I only used 1/4 cup sugar and that was plenty especially when using a dressing which I completely recommend over regular mayo, plus it's much healthier.  The salad smells like eggs although they don't overwhelm the recipe. Each ingredient has a subtle flavor that comes out in every bite. The dill pickle relish is a great addition and really boosted the flavor. I added half of the dressing mixture to the macaroni, let sit overnight then added about half of the remaining.  Essentially, you really only need about 3/4 of the dressing, but then again, to each his own. Thanks for the recipe! This is definitely a keeper!

text:
Very good base recipe for any salad.  However, I would limit the amount of sugar up to 1/4 cup.  For my liking, 1/4 cup is the max limit that I can possibly add sugar (I can even do without sugar at all).  I would even limit to 1/8 cup next time.  The level of sweetness with 1/4 cup was similar to the KFC coleslaw.  So it was pretty sweet, but not too sweet.  You can add whatever the chopped veggies as you like; I used olives since I had no dill pickles relish.  Added chopped cucumbers and carrots for color.  Will make it again :)

country:

text:
My fiance loved this recipe, and while I had to make some changes I think it worked very well. Being British, I've never used sugar in a savoury dish before (this is something more commonly found in US recipes) so I was wary of the 3/4 cup given for the ingredients. I ended up just using around 1/4 of a cup of sugar as per suggestions from other reviewers, which worked in a good balance with the white vinegar. Since I wasn't able to get hold of American mustard (and believe me, you do not want 3 T of British or French mustard in this dish, it's far too strong!) I used 1 cup of mustard mayonnaise and 1 cup of 3% fat mayonnaise, which worked really well together. I couldn't find any dill pickle relish so I chopped up a couple of pickled gherkins and added 1 T of the juice from their jar, which stopped the sauce from being too thick. I also used a red onion rather than a normal one to give the dish some more colour, and added some spring onion and cubes of cheddar cheese. The celery seeds (a new discovery for me) worked really well in the sauce and I'll definitely be using them again in other dishes. I'm looking forward to experimenting with this recipe and seeing what other variants I can create. This a good basis for a standard macaroni salad and is one of those recipes you can change around depending on availability of ingredients and personal preferences and it still turns out well.

text:
This recipe has been one in my box for almost a year and finally I made it for a BBQ we had this weekend. Wow...have I ever been missing one of the best macaroni salads I've ever tasted...why did I wait so long? I pretty much followed the recipe except for reducing the sugar, I just  kept tasting the dressing until it reached the sweetness desired, probably even less than 1/4 cup. I left the onion out, not my preference but some of our guest do not like raw onions, so I added green pepper along with the red. Used cider vinegar and used Kraft light olive oil mayo. The dressing absolutely takes this mac salad over the five stars. I made early and let it sit all day in the fridge, reserving about a half cup of the dressing, added that in to make creamy for our serving time at dinner. The reviews were very helpful and suggest you read through some. It makes quite a bit which is a good thing since seconds were requested by our guests.

This is definitely a fantastic summer addition!

Cook up the macaroni up to a week or more and freeze it. When ready to use, rinse under cold water and drain. By doing this, macaroni does not absorb the dressing and it tastes like you just cooked it. I do this with all pasta.

text:
I read a lot of the reviews before making this.  I had to make it for a large crowd.  I was pretty much able to double everything except I only used 1 large red pepper.  I minced the onion, celery and pepper fine so there wouldn't be large chunks of the veggies.  I added about 1 cup of finely shredded carrot for color.  I only had sweet pickle relish and I only used 2 Tbsp. of that so it wouldn't be overpowering.  I used 8 eggs. I used 1/2 cup of sugar in the dressing (remember I doubled the recipe) and cut the mustard to 2-3  Tbsp.  I used cider vinger and added some black pepper and garlic powder.  I didn't have celery seed so I had to use celery salt and cut the amount down.  I made this the afternoon before my function.  I added just enough dressing to moisten at that time, then added some more before going to bed.  I added the rest of the dressing the next morning and it needed every bit of it.  I ended up making 1 more batch of dressing but only needed about 1/4 of it to moisten at the party I took it to.  I'll use the extra dressing for egg salad or potato salad.  I had quite a few people ask me for the recipe but my mother-in-law just had to tell me "it was o.k. but it was too sweet".  No surprise there, she critiques everything I make! I will definitely make this again but would try to cut the prep down by boiling the  eggs and making the dressing ahead of time.  Thanks for a great recipe!

Different than the tuna mac I am used to making but very good. I have made it twice in 3 days and both times upped it to serve 9, first time I only had a few tablespoons left after all was said and done. text:
I absolutley love this recipe but I did make some changes.  They are as follows: I used mini bowtie pasta (about 10 oz. dried), used 3/4 cup mayo, 2 Tbs dijon mustard, used 1/2 cup onion, omitted the red pepper and used 1 serrano pepper instead (balances the sweetness with a kick), used 1/4 tsp. celery salt & 1/4 tsp. garlic salt, dropped the sugar down to 1/4 cup and also omitted the vinegar.  I also only used 1 large stalk of celery and added a little pimiento for color.  So I guess you can say I made a lot of little changes but used this as a base/guideline, (I did use 3 hardboiled eggs though) it really turned out excellent.  Also, as other reviewers have mentioned (thank you) it's pretty darn sweet using only 1/4 cup sugar, I would definitely start with that amount and if you feel it needs to be sweeter for whatever reason add more after tasting.

After reading the other reviews, I decided that Miracle Whip wasn't the right choice.  So I made this recipe and substituted mayo (low fat) instead.  I also reduced the sugar to 2/3 c. (used half Splenda and half sugar).  I substituted carrots for the green pepper as that's what I had and my DH doesn't care for gr. pepper.  I really think you could use any veggies your family prefers.  I also added diced leftover turkey to turn this into a lite summer main dish and served it with sliced tomatoes and cornbread.  It was a real hit.  I think you can't go wrong with this salad if you use mayo.  Then it is definitely worth the 5 stars.  My hubby L O V E D this salad. I will definitly keep this one.

text:
I was leary of this recipe.  I've never had Amish macaroni salad and unfortunately thought it (for whatever illogical reason) was supposed to have a ton of sugar.  I also prefer not pre-reading reviews so as not to be influenced by them.  My mistake.  I was actually surprised it wasn't any more sweet than it was. I sort of got used to it but didn't want to make it again.    After reading reviews, and because it just makes sense, I'm inclined to believe the sugar thing is a typo.  I disagree that it's too much dressing, as I usually do, but I always chill mine and the dressing always soaks in.  Most pasta recipes don't have enough sauce IMO.  I might try this again, and look up some other recipes to see what the "Amish" kind is supposed to be like.  However, I must say that after almost 150 reviews, wouldn't the original poster have "checked in" and fixed it if it was a typo???
EDIT:   I made this again, assuming 3/4 TSP. sugar, and that made it way too mustardy.  I did buy some at the deli and it was nothing like this recipe.

text:
I grew up on macaroni salad made with tuna and Hellmann's so this recipe was quite different than what I am used to...and exactly why I wanted to try it!  I have to say, this kind of reminds me of the stuff I get at the deli when I am in a pinch, only this recipe is much much better (the guys at the deli must use miracle whip too).  As per the reviews, I cut back on the sugar a lot and only used 1 tablespoon which was plenty.  Also, I made two minor changes.  In place of the celery seed and salt called for in the recipe,I used 1 teaspoon of celery salt instead and because the grocery store didn't sell dill relish I decided to just mince up a a dill pickle.  It is a nice alternative to the macaroni salad my family and I are used to having :)

I love how people totally change the recipe then rate it. I grew up in NW Pennsylvania eating authentic cooking from my Amish neighbors. This recipe, made exactly as written, is AMISH Macaroni Salad! It is sweet as most is, it is made with Miracle Whip; it has celery. If you don't like it, rate as so, and move on to a non-Amish version. Save you add-in's / leave out's for your own recipe instead of ruining this for someone searching for the real thing.

text:
Loved it!!  Best Mac salad recipe I've had.  Will be a permanent fixture on my summer menu.  Having said that, and after reading the reviews I made just a few slight tweaks.  I really don't like too sweet of a salad of any type, so I only added 2 Tbsp. of sugar which was perfect for my buds, and used apple cider vinegar instead of white.  I didn't have red pepper, so I used the green pepper that I had on hand. I had plenty of celery but no celery seeds so I put in 4 stalks of celery so their was plenty of flavor, and this worked out well.  I also used Best Foods mayonaise, as i am not a miracle whip girl! And this is my preferred brand.  I made it tonight, used just over a cup of mayo.  I'd imagine I may be adding a bit more in am as the mayo was absorbed by the pasta.  I look forward to the next time Ii make it, as i will have the proper called for ingredients on hand and try it just as in recipe except for the called for amount of sugar.  

Thank you Connie for such a delicious treat!!!  Best recipe ever!!

text:
No sugar, no vinegar. Use miracle whip and real mayonnaise. If the recipe calls for 2 cups of mayo or whip, just adjust the recipe, use 1 cup mayo and 1 cup miracle whip. Extra eggs do not hurt. If you like them add them. More eggs mean more mayo/whip........    Remember, the longer the salad has to wait for serving, the eggs and macaroni will absorb the mayonnaise and miracle whip. Just add more of each until it is to your preferred consistency. You do not need celery seed either. For a kick add 1 T worcestshire. :)

I recommend using Hellman's mayo.  The first time I made this with Miracle Whip I cut the sugar to 1/4 cup. I should add that I am a mayo person rather than a MW person and my mayo of choice is Hellman's(or Best Foods here in Phoenix).

I decided on this pasta salad to serve at my daughters 2nd birthday party. It was wonderful. I took other reviewers advice and cut the amount sugar. I used Miracle Whip dressing and apple cider vinegar in place of regular vinegar. I also used bowties instead of macaroni and used the whole box, not just 2 cups. Do make sure if you are making this ahead to only add half of the cream mixture to the pasta, reserving the other half to be added just before serving. This ensures a wonderful, creamy pasta salad.

text:
Look no further, this truly is the best macaroni salad! I've made this many times and just decided to change my old review- The 1st time I made it I thought it was too saucy, so then I'd make it w/ half the sauce, but I've since decided I think it's better as written- it really soaks it up over time. Because of this it's best the next day, I think. You can easily adjust, add or omit ingredients to suit your taste, but as written it's a perfect 'classic' macaroni salad... I like to use reduced fat mayo, add 1ts/ea. dry mustard and dry dill, and 1/2ts celery salt instead of seed, cut the sugar to 1/2 cup and use sweet relish, sometimes sub 2 finely chopped fresh jalapenos for red pepper. This is waaay better than the store bought deli kind and is a quick, simple, cheap side dish. Keeps well in the frige for a couple days, so make the full amount...

Not that this recipe needs another 5 star review but I think this is the best macaroni salad that I have ever tasted.  My husband loves pasta salads but I could never make them until I found this recipe.  Now I make it all the time.  The only changes to this recipe I would suggest is to start out with only 1/2 the amount of ingredients for the dressing mix unless you like soupy pasta (you can always add more later if you want), use Best Foods (that's the only kind of mayo I use), and start with only 1/8 cup of sugar, you can add more according to your taste.  I added sliced black olives and used 1/2 the red bell pepper just for color.  This macaroni salad though is AWESOME!!!

This is super and my family LOVED it, but the proportions are off. There is way too much dressing for the amount of pasta. I used a full 16 ounce package and had a super creamy macaroni salad. I left out the eggs (I just don't prefer them in my pasta salads). I was also out of relish so I finely diced some dill pickles and I cut the sugar back to 1/2 cup and it was plenty sweet. When I made it and tasted it, I thought it was good, but it is much better if you let chill for an hour or so - the flavors come together much better and it goes from good to fantastic! Even sitting in the refrigerator for a couple of hours, it never dried out like some macaroni salads do. It stayed very creamy. I will make this again!!

text:
I made this recipe as 4 servings for my partner and I to try out before I make it for my son's first birthday in two weeks. This has to be the best macaroni salad I have ever had, and I would consider myself somewhat of a macaroni salad connisseur. 
I did make a few changes with the ingrediants: (For 4 servings)
1-1/3 cup macaroni uncooked
2 hard boiled eggs, diced
1/4 cup green onion, diced
2 stalks celery, diced
1/3 cup red pepper, diced
1-1/2 tbsp dill relish
1-1/3 cup fat free Miracle Whip
1-1/2 tbsp mustard
1/3 cup white sugar
1-1/2 tbsp white wine vinegar
1/4 tsp celery salt

Next time I do make this recipe (2 weeks from now!) I plan on only putting half the sauce over the macaroni, and leaving it over night, and then adding more dressing as needed before serving.

Overall this a pretty good macaroni salad recipe.  We also did some minor alterations:  We used  regular mayo and cut it back to about 1-1/2 (you can also use some non-fat yogurt to cut down on the calories, but I had none available) add mayo for proper consistency.  I also used some colorful curled rotini noodles with the standard elbow for a change.  And added about 1/3 cup of Italian salad dressing, about a tablespoon of chopped fresh parsley, a few shakes of paprika for presentation.  Because of all the negative experience everyone had with sugar, I added none.  This tasted like a potato salad, which is what I was striving for anyhow.  Good recipe.  Ill be making this again!

This recipe is great! Just like my Ohio grandma's macaroni salad.  What's nice about this recipe is that as long as you have the basics you can add/reduce to adjust to your taste. text:
It is not often you find a flavor combination that appeals to almost everyone. This recipe does indeed.  I 
reduced my sugar to 2 T.  I also used
nonfat mayo (Just-2Good 3 cups) and I used 1 cup Miracle Whip.  I doubled
the recipe.  I omitted the salt but I
heavily salted my noodles as is my practice.  I did not use the celery seed as I have found it to be a little overpowering for my taste as a rule.  The chopped celery is a must tho, unless you just happen to hate celery.  I as another poster found that I olny needed half the dressing mix and was thankful I hadn't poured it on all at once.  I will add this recipe to my book of favorite recipes.
The next time I make this I am going to add some small cubes of cheese as I think it will taste great with all the flavors.  I may also try adding in some breast of chicken, tuna, or some salmon for a main-meal salad.
Thank you Connie for a great recipe.
Don't be shy,give this one a try.

This was just delicious, but I altered the recipe a bit adding much less sugar as other recommended. I made a double batch as we had quite a few people coming over for a barbecue. text:
I have never written a review before but this is just the best pasta salad ever!!! and, I am not a fan of pasta salads. I enjoyed this at a friend's recently and had to try it. Luckily I read the reviews and made adjustments per the reviews. For sure, add another egg and decrease the amount of sugar, for me 1/4 cup was way enough. I also added cayenne pepper because , well, I love cayenne. The most important thing is, as noted in the reviews, only add "mayo" or Miracle Whip sparingly at first, you can always add more later, like the next day.Another tip, I learned about many years ago from my ex mother in law, Dill pickle juice!!!!!! She taught me this secret to use in potato salad and I have used it ever since.The key to this recipe seems to be to add condiments to the consistency that you like.

text:
This stuff is amazing and I always get lots of raves when I take it somewhere!!  I have been making it since last summer & have made my own changes to the original recipe.  First, I cut back on the sugar to just shy a 1/2 cup.  I also cook an entire box (full pound) of pasta because 2 cups is nothing and I think the ratio is better.  This brings me to my next change.  I use a twisty pasta like Gemelli rather than traditional elbow macaroni - the twists help absorb up some of the extra dressing (of which there is PLENTY).  Finally, I despise celery seed so I leave that out (there is already celery in it so I don't think it's necessary).

Delicious.  I would have rated five stars but i made a few minor changes.  I cut the sugar just a little.  I'm used to sweet macaroni salad, so the amt in the recipe wasn't that bad to me.  I omitted the celery seed because i don't care for it.  I actually made this 2 days in advance and it improved in taste each day.  However, it start to dry out after the 1st day. So, i added plain mayonnaise to make it creamier. The mayonnaise actually improved the taste to me.  So, if i made again and was going to use immediately, I'd probably substitue about 1/2 C of the miracle whip with mayo.

text:
Good recipe but sugar has to be according to taste. I started with 1/4 and kept adding until it tasted right. Next time I will do that same thing with the vinegar, start with 1 tsp. and keep adding from there. Used 4 eggs. The dressing was too much for 2 cups of uncooked macaroni. Good thing I added an extra cup and a handful (for luck). The dressing was enough for all this. Last bit of advice, I made the dressing first, tasted, added eggs, tasted, then added macaroni a bit at a time, looking for the right amount of 'dryness'. My husband loves the Amish macaroni salad from WalMart, this was what I was trying to copy. The final result we compared with a helping of the store made. He says mine was exactly the same, I say mine was a little tangier. He said this recipe was 'better'.

text:
Pretty good! While I prefer Graden's classic macaroni salad a *touch* better, this was also quite good. This is a very heavy, mayonnaise-laden salad (if you're not a fan, continue your search for a recipe that better suits your tastes). Graden'saversion is lightly dressed and has a less creamy texture (her dressing is a bit runny in comparison). Both salads have a sweet aftertaste that makes them VERY similar. NOTE: As many others have done, I too dressed my salad with HALF of my dressing and saved the rest to add as I saw fit. I also reduced the sugar to 1/2 c. and was pleased with the result (3/4 c. sugar would be overkill, IMHO). All in all, I found this to be yummy and a great contribution to the fish fry dinner my hubs and I were invited to. Actually, I have been requested to make this (again) for our upcoming block party next month! Thanks for sharing, Connie! :-)

Wow! This is simply amazing!
We found that the onino was almost too overpowering. Green onion would be a better pairing. The egg also got lost in the salad, so I added one more that I had already made. In addition, there was so much dressing, so I added another 2 cups of pasta and 2 stalks of celery. Took reviewer's advice and cut sugar down to 1/2 cup. I did not have enough miracle whip, so I used 1 cup miracle whip and 1 cup mayonnaise. This had a fantastic taste. I think I will split the two from now on. It changed the flavour and balance the zip and plainness of the two dressings. Thank-you so much for the recipe!

text:
Very good recipe! This is the first time I've ever made home made macaroni salad and this one was the closest to what I liked, but I still changed it up a bit. Instead of just 2 cups of macaroni, I used a whole 16 oz box, so I didn't have any "soupy" problems like other reviewers. Also I used 4 eggs, 1 stalk of celery (not really a fan), used a green pepper, cut up 2 dill pickles since I had no relish, and like others said definitely cut the sugar to 1/4 cup!! I'm so glad I read the reviews first because it's still a little sweet for me, but everyone else loved it! Also I didn't have celery seed. Still a fantastic recipe and one I'll use many more times. For me, this was a perfect starting point.

text:
Absolutely delicious.  Used whole wheat pasta because that's the only thing I had on hand.  Used real mayo (1.5 cups) and 1/2 cup of maple syrup instead of the sugar.  Used old-fashioned whole grain mustard.  Instead of the red pepper, I used blanched broccoli.  And I substituted leftover rotisserie chicken for the egg.  So the onion wouldn't be so strong, I let them sit in a bowl of cold water for a few minutes.  I really enjoyed this.

text:
I wanted to find a new macaroni salad recipe because when I make it from scratch myself, I tend to use the same ingredients as my potato salad. Even though I make a fantastic potato salad, I wanted a different taste. This is absolutely the most amazing macaroni salad I have ever had in my life. I always read the reviews before I make a recipe, and usually find myself irritated by the people who change the recipe before first trying the original version. I am now guilty of doing just that. So many people said this was too sweet, so I took some changes from different reviews and proceeded to make the best macaroni salad my family has ever had. Thank you Connie0751 for giving us this amazing recipe, and please accept my apologies for making the following changes: I didn't use Miracle Whip at all, but used real mayonnaise instead. I used apple cider vinegar instead of white vinegar. I only used 3 tablespoons white sugar, and because I like spicy tasting food I diced 1/2 cup of radishes and added to the mix. A lot of reviewers complained that the recipe made a very soupy salad. I was not serving it until the next day anyway, and like a lot of reviewers said, by then it had soaked into the pasta and was absolutely perfect! I will make this my go-to salad from now on, I am completely addicted!!

I was worried about the taste because of the different ingredients used, but I was very surprised by the flavor of this dish.  It was really good and I got many positive comments.  The changes I made per other reviewers were:  used one box of small sea shell pasta, added one extra egg, only used 1/4 cup sugar, used cider vinegar vice white vinegar and added a dash of pepper.  Since I added so much pasta, I think I should have doubled the sauce as it was a little dry.  I prefer to have a more creamy macaroni salad. Will be making again for the 4th of July cookout.

text:
This recipe is absolutely delicious. After making it a few times, and following some of the other reviews, I have concluded the following: The best way to eat is the day after. So, make this dish a day in advance, pasta and all, and you'll love it.  Don't mix all the pasta at once because it will be too soupy.  It calls for too much sugar, therefore, taste as you're mixing the sugar to make sure that it is to your liking. I have a sweet tooth and it was way too much for me the first time. I upped the eggs to 5 and only used one tabblespoon of mustard.  I can eat this by itself, but not without refrigeration as some of the ingredients give it a really strong taste before blending.

text:
This salad rocks!! I made some modifications  based on personal preference and the result, in my opinion, was fabulous! I used 3C (12 oz) macaroni and kept the dressing measurements the same. It was the perfect amount.For the dressing, I used regular mayo, decreased the sugar to 1/3 C and the mustard to 2T.I adjusted the salt to suit my taste, added fresh ground pepper, and omitted the celery seed. For the salad,I used 5 eggs, cut back on all the veggies to about 1/2 of what's called for, as I didn't want them to overwhelm the taste of the salad. I also used 3T sweet relish rather than dill, red and yellow peppers, added a small can of sliced black olives and some dried parsley flakes for color. It looked beautifuly colorful and tasted great. A keeper for sure.

You might find yourself wondering "how different can a macaroni salad be?"  Well, this one is delicious!!!!  I haven't ever been a fan of macaroni salad because it seems like they dry out after a day in the fridge but this one only gets better!  I think the celery seed is a must.  If you don't have any on hand go get some...it makes the salad very flavorful.  Also, I agree that the 3/4 cup of sugar is too much.  I used 1/3 cup and it was PLENTY sweet.  My husband doesn't like dill pickle relish in salad so I used sweet, also very good.  My daughter-in-law doesn't usually like pasta of any kind and she had seconds of this.  I will make this over and over again.  Maybe next time with some orange, red and yellow bell pepper for added color.

text:
I love this stuff! Macaroni salad has always been a favorite of mine. I made this with just a couple of changes. I only had 1/2 the celery on hand that was called for and next time I'll make sure I have enough on hand before I start. I don't care for the little red pepper so I left that out. I used a dill pickle cut up instead of the sweet relish. The only thing I would change next time is to use a little more onion than called for and about half as much sugar. It's good as is but I think it would be just as good with about half as much sugar. Also, this makes a LOT of salad but that was ok by me since I love the left overs. But be aware that it makes about twice as many servings as listed. Thank you Connie for posting one of the best mac salad recipes I've tasted.

text:
I made this for a large BBQ party as a side so I tripled this and made the following changes and/or substitutions: Due to multiple guests needing gluten free dishes, I used gluten free spiral pasta. I omitted the celery, bell pepper, and celery seed. I used sweet relish instead of dill. I sauted the onion in butter seasoned with a little salt, sugar, all spice, and garlic powder until translucent. Also, I  used 4 cups total of Miracle Whip as opposed to the 6 cups the recipe would have warranted.  And I used a total of a  cup of sugar, so in actuality I used a third less sugar then called for. It was a hit! Several people asked for the recipe which I gladly shared! I will be adding this to my go to recipes!

I have made this several times so, I feel I can give a proper review. The first time I made it like I tend to do, I followed the instructions to a "T". We all thought it was a little to sweet. I make it to take family functions and everyone raves over it. Thank you for such a wonderful recipe.

This was, quite simply, the best macaroni salad I've eaten and will be my "Go To" recipe now!  I did make a couple of minor changes for personal preferences:  I used real Best Food Mayo vs. Miracle Whip, and decreased the amount of sugar by about a half  as I like a more savory salad (and dislike M.W.) text:
I've made this quite a few times.  Each time it seems I'm short on one ingredient or another and have improvised.  This time I used gluten free rice and flax elbow macaroni, olive oil miracle whip instead of the regular, chopped dill pickles in place of the dill relish as well as 3 chopped scallions in place of the regular white onion I typically use.  It's just as delicious as ever.  It's a great recipe to double for larger cookouts or groups as well and I've often made it a day or two ahead for such occasions.  There's never any leftovers!

Wow! This is like my mom used to make; it is absolutely delicious. 
I read the reviews and reduced the sugar to just under 1/4 cup and it was perfect for my tastes. Also heeded the advice of not adding all of the dressing and refrigerating it to add the next day, glad I did that!

So yummy; thank-you for sharing this recipe!

The point of a recipe is to make it easier for you to balance the amounts of each ingredient.  This recipe fails at that in a spectacular way.  As posted, it calls for an insane amount if sugar.  I cut it to 1/2 a cup when I saw the gruesome pile of sweet starting to stack up in the mixing bowl but I was trying to have faith in the recipe. text:
Was looking for the familiar taste of Pennsylvania Dutch macaroni salad from my childhood and found it!  I doubled the ingredients and had about half a cup of pasta left in the box so I added it. I stuck with regular mayo and half the sugar.  It was still a bit sweet from what I remember. It's liquidy, but will be perfect after sitting a few hours. I'll update after dinner, but was so excited I had to say thanks!

I forgot to update (probably because there was none left to remind me)!  None of my California friends has experienced the vinegar/ sweet combo in this type of dish and they loved it.  It was much less watery after sitting a few hours. Doubled the recipe again but went with half the sugar and regular mayo. Perfect!  This is a dish that has to have time for the flavors to blend.

I wouldn't suggest reducing the sauce because when setting the macaroni soaks up the juice, so what appears at first to be too much, actually ends up being perfect. Delicious.

text:
This is my go-to macaroni salad recipe. With just a few adjustments, I think it comes out perfectly. I use a whole pound of elbow macaroni, and cook it as the submitter suggests (bring water to boil. add macaroni. stir. remove from heat. cover and let sit for 10 minutes. then drain, rinse with cold water, and put aside). I bought a 15oz jar of whipped dressing, then just added a tbsp of mayo. I also cut the sugar to 1/2 cup, and increased the salt to about 1/2 tsp. It's still a bit sweet, but balanced a little more with the extra salt. I also added an extra egg, just because. I think it tastes similar to our local grocery store's Amish macaroni salad (which I love), and the no-cook dressing makes this recipe nice and simple. Especially good if made ahead, and refrigerated overnight :)

text:
Husband loves amish potato and macaroni salad because it is quite sweet.  So far, out of all the amish style recipes we have tried, this is his favorite.  In fact, it got a thumbs up from everyone at the table, which is unusual at our house. I did not alter the recipe measurements, but I did use mayo rather than salad dressing.  I also put the chopped celery and peppers to the side so that they could add them at the table.  I offered dill weed and smoked paprika at the table to top it off as well.

There was a lot of extra dressing but by tomorrow I am sure it will have been absorbed by the noodles.  It was quite sweet but the dill pickle relish provided a nice contrast to the sweetness. 

This will become one of our go to macaroni salad recipes.  Thank you for a great recipe!

Delicious and easy. I usually just buy macaroni salad from the deli and go from there, but this time I used whole grain macaroni and made the dressing from scratch. Like others I cut down on the sugar but used sweet pickle relish instead for more sweetness. I used a 16 oz box of elbow macaroni but next time I will try bow ties. I cut the amount of dressing in half, and used mayonnaise, seasoned salt and celery seed but no celery. I also like macaroni salad with small cubes of white cheddar (1/4 pound) and 1 cup of defrosted frozen petite peas. It's only been chilling for a while but it tastes great. This recipe is very flexible and accomodates what you have on hand.

text:
This makes a lot if you're like us and it's just the two of you you'll want to half the recipe. It made more sauce than I needed so I boiled up & diced a potato - makes a decent potato salad as well. Also I could see this sauce on a vegetable platter for dipping.

I am glad I read the reviews. Like most here I reduced the sugar. {You can always add more but you can't take it out} I used 1/4 cup sugar and still a bit sweet for me. I'll do 1/8 next time and it'll be perfect.

I also shredded a carrot for additional color, I didn't have yellow mustard so I used Spicy Brown mustard. I used Malt Vinegar not white, and I ran out of Miracle Whip so it was 1 cup MW and 1 cup mayonnaise. And like everyone I added an extra egg.

I love this recipe because it's flexible. Next time I might throw in some thawed frozen peas, maybe diced ham or some tuna. Smoked Paprika maybe? This recipee accommodates a lot of variety, be creative or just clean out the fidge of leftovers.

text:
Oh yes! This is just the taste I was craving!  I had no relish so I chopped up a few baby dills.  I used red onion, and I added a bit of black pepper.
In an attempt to make a somewhat healthier version, I also made the following substitutions:
-I used Stevia sweetener instead of sugar, equivalent to 1/2 cup sugar
-I replaced the Miracle Whip with 1 part canola oil mayo, 2 parts plain nonfat Greek yogurt, and a splash of lime juice
-I replaced the traditional elbow macaroni with veggie radiatori, used a 12 oz package
-I used 4 eggs, but replaced half of the yolks with avocado
It's good now.  I know it will be GREAT tomorrow!  I can hardly wait...

text:
The amount of sugar called for by the original recipe is perplexing.  The first time I made it I cut the sugar in half and found it nearly inedible; it was far, far too sweet for my family's tastes.  I've made it several times since, replacing the dressing with real mayo, adding a bit of celery salt, using cider vinegar instead of white and eliminating the sugar completely.  My family absolutely loves this recipe with these changes.

It may seem like far too much dressing when first made, but the macaroni absorbs most of this by the second day.  Cutting back the dressing makes it less "soupy" the first day but a bit dry for left-overs.  It's delicious on day one but far better on the second day in my opinion!

text:
I wondered how this macaroni salad could be that much better than the usual kind, but it is! The egg is a really nice touch. My husband made the same comment a couple of other reviewers made on here: "I don't even like macaroni salad, but this was awesome!". I brought it to a party and everyone loved it. I do wish I had used a sweeter onion (the one I used was a little strong). I followed the suggestion of others and cut down on the sugar. Because I used regular mayo I used 1/2 cup (if I'd used Miracle Whip I would have gone down to 1/4 cup because it's already so sweet). Even the 1/2 cup was almost too sweet, so I definitely would not use the amount in the recipe. I used less celery, bell pepperand onion than the recipe called for because it seemed like too much...but if you like your macaroni salad crunchy then you would probably want to go with the recommended amount. Other than that, I wouldn't change a thing. Thanks so much for the recipe, I WILL be making it often!

This has to be one of the best Macaroni Salad recipes I've had!
I found it to be too much dressing for the amount of pasta so I either cut the dressing recipe in half or if I'm making it for a pot luck I double the pasta I use.
I also cut back on the sugar to 1/4 cup for the full recipe.
I saute my onion in 1tsp of olive oil for 5 minutes and use 1 whole roasted red pepper, jarred works great.I don't always add the eggs and it still tastes great.
This salad is always a big hit where ever I bring it with kids and adults!

i made this salad for a pot luck of 10 ppl. it looked great and everyone was really exicted to try it. it was ok. nothing special, i added only 1/4 c of sugar b/c i like tangy instead of sweet mac salad. i think it was a little bland, i put in a lot more salt. my dressing i used Renee's Ceaser dressing and i think that made it taste a lot better. i don't think i will make this again - there just just nothing special about it.
